The response is either sufficiency with a certain aspect of tasawwur? meaning that what is meant by the invalidity of division before definition is that dividing something before knowing it in some respect is invalid, and it does not apply here because knowledge is known to minds in some respect, or because the definition of knowledge, etc. (Abd) It was said: the speaker is Imam al-Razi: the point of weakness is that knowledge being self-evident does not entail that one should not alert to it in the context of division, for it may also be obscure. So to remove obscurity and determine the divided thing, alerting to it is necessary. The self-evident in belief: Know that belief in a relation either leaves room for other possibility, then the predominant is suspicion, the overwhelmed is delusion, and doubt if they are equal; or it leaves no room, then it is categorical, then it is compound ignorance if it does not correspond to reality; if it corresponds, then it is imitation if it disappears with the doubt of a doubter, and if it does not disappear, it is certainty. So delusion and doubt are from the tasawwurat, and the rest are from the tasdiqat. (Ismail with addition) 'He chose' means when he made tasdiq the same as assent, he chose the position of the ancient philosophers. Sayyid al-Sind said in his glosses on Sharh al-Shamsiyya: This is the truth. (Abd) Explanation of tasdiq and tasawwur: 'Otherwise, it is tasawwur.' And the judgment (hukm) is not the composite consisting of it and the conception of the two extremes as Imam al-Razi claimed. And he chose the position of the ancients who made the object of assent and the judgment, which is the last part of the proposition, the affirmative or negative predicative relation, not the occurrence or non-occurrence of the attributive relation, because the author will later refer to the tripartite division of the proposition in the discussions of propositions. His saying 'Otherwise, it is tasawwur' whether it is an apprehension of a single thing, like the conception of Zayd. (The two extremes) and there is a consideration: for tasdiq according to the Imam is composed of three conceptions and the judgment, so the relation must be mentioned, as is obvious, unless it is said that he omitted it relying on the sound nature, or that what is meant by 'the two extremes' is with the relation connecting them. (Ismail) His saying 'claimed' indicates the weakness of the Imam's position. Its explanation as Sayyid al-Sind said: each of tasawwur and tasdiq is distinct from the other by a specific path, so in the division of knowledge, that distinction must be observed, and that observation is visible in their manner of division but not in his division. (Ismail) The relation: if he had said 'relation of conjunction or non-conjunction' or 'relation of disjunction or non-disjunction', the conditional tasdiqat would not have been excluded. I say: since the origin of the conditional is the categorical with the addition of tools of conjunction and disjunction, his saying 'the affirmative or negative predicative relation' includes the conditionals as well. (Muhashi) From 'Zayd'? 'Non-occurrence' means what he made the object of assent is the occurrence of the relation, etc., as is the case with the later scholars. Know that all the philosophers after agreeing that tasdiq is simple, for it is assent and judgment, differed over whether the object of assent is the affirmative or negative predicative relation or the occurrence or non-occurrence of the attributive relation. The ancients chose the first and said with tripartite division of the proposition: the subject, the predicate, and the affirmative or negative predicative relation. And this is the truth, for from 'standing' for example, only one relation is understood, and it does not need another relation for its connection. And tasdiq according to them is another type of apprehension, different from tasawwur by essential difference, not by consideration of the object. The later scholars went to the second and said with quadripartite division of the proposition: the subject, the predicate, the attributive relation (whether affirmative or negative) which they call the judgmental relation that is the locus of judgment in the sense of the complete predicative relation, and the fourth is a predicative relation which is its occurrence or non-occurrence. Unless it is said that they did not intend to prove two essentially different relations. (Abd) He will later refer when he says in the discussion of propositions: the subject is called the subject, the predicate is called the predicate, and the indicator of the relation is the copula. Whether the negation applies to the whole of his saying 'assent to the relation' such that the divisions of tasawwur are also restricted.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening of a text on logic, likely Tahzeeb al-Mantiq. It addresses the definition of knowledge ('ilm) and its division into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). The commentator explains that if knowledge involves assenting to a relation (nisba) in a proposition, it is tasdiq; otherwise, it is tasawwur. He notes that the author did not explicitly define 'ilm, giving three possible reasons: either because tasawwur is sufficient for the purpose of division, or because the definition is well-known, or because knowledge is self-evident. The commentator then discusses the nature of tasdiq, siding with the ancient philosophers (hukama') who consider tasdiq to be the act of assenting (idh'an) to the predicative relation, whether affirmative or negative. He contrasts this with the view of Imam al-Razi, who considered tasdiq to include the entire proposition (subject, predicate, and judgment). The commentator argues that tasdiq is simple, not composite, and that the judgment is only the relation, not the entire proposition. The passage also delves into the division of propositions: the ancients held a tripartite structure (subject, predicate, relation), while the later scholars added a fourth element (the occurrence or non-occurrence of the attributive relation). The commentator favors the tripartite view, stating that only one relation is needed. The discussion includes clarifications on terms like 'aql (intellect) and the various types of belief (certainty, doubt, etc.). The parenthetical names (Abd, Ismail, Muhashi) are likely marginal glosses or commentary references.

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq is a simple act of assenting to a relation, not a composite of multiple conceptions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Construct a brief argument defending the commentator's position that tasdiq is simple, using an example from fiqh (e.g., 'Zakat is wajib'). Show that the judgment is the key element, not the concepts of zakat and wajib.

What Is Mantiq?

Tripartite vs Quadripartite Structure of Propositions
Commentary compares tripartite and quadripartite views of proposition structure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the ancient (tripartite) and later (quadripartite) views on the components of a proposition, and evaluate which is more coherent.

Core Idea
A proposition consists of subject, predicate, and relation — not four parts.

The passage discusses a key disagreement among logicians: do propositions have three parts (subject, predicate, predicative relation) or four parts (adding the occurrence or non-occurrence of an attributive relation)? The commentator favors the tripartite view of the ancient philosophers. This lesson unpacks that debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the tripartite view
Find where the passage says 'the ancients chose the first and said with tripartite division of the proposition: the subject, the predicate, and the affirmative or negative predicative relation.' Understand that they consider the relation (nisba) as a single component.
2
Identify the quadripartite view
Locate 'the later scholars went to the second and said with quadripartite division of the proposition: the subject, the predicate, the attributive relation, and a fourth predicative relation which is its occurrence or non-occurrence.'
3
Understand the commentator's preference
The commentator says 'this is the truth' referring to the tripartite view. He argues that from 'standing' only one relation is understood, so a second relation is unnecessary.
4
Apply to a real proposition
Take the proposition 'The world is created'. According to the tripartite view, the parts are: subject (world), predicate (created), and the relation (predicative affirmative relation). According to the quadripartite view, you would also have an attributive relation linking 'created' to 'world' and then the occurrence of that relation.
Example from kalam: the proposition 'The world is temporally originated' – try to break it down both ways.

إن كان إذعانا للنسبة فتصديق، تعريف العلم الحاصلة من الشيء عند العقل، والمصنف له لم يتعرض لتعريفه؛ إما للاكتفاء بالتصور بوجه ما في مقام التقسيم وإما لأن تعريف العلم مشهور مستفيض وإما لأن العلم بديهي التصور على ما قيل. قوله: إن كان إذعانا للنسبة أي اعتقادا بالنسبة الخبرية الثبوتية كالإذعان بأن زيدا قائم أو السلبية، كالاعتقاد بأنه ليس بقائم، فقد اختار مذهب الحكماء حيث جعل التصديق نفس الإذعان الحاصلة أن العلم هو الصورة الناشئة المنتزعة منه سواء كانت له أو لا. وإنما عدل عن التعريف يعني المشهور، وهو حصول صورة الشيء في العقل؛ لأن المنقسم إلى التصور والتصديق هو العلم الكاسب والمكتسب، كما هو الظاهر الظاهر من ملاحظة غرض هذا الفن، والحصول معنى لا دخل له في الاكتساب مع أن الحصول ليس معنى حقيقيا للعلم، كيف والعلم عبارة عن الانكشاف ونعلم بداهةً أنه إذا حصل الصورة في نفسها حصل الانكشاف ولا تحتاج إلى انتزاع معنى الحصول عنها. هذا ما يذهب إليه النظر الجلي، وأما النظر الدقيق على ما قال فيحكم بأن المراد بحصول الصورة المعنى الحاصل بالمصدر، وحقيقته ما يعبر عنه بالفارسية بـ"دانش"، حالة إدراكية تحقق عند حصول الشيء في الذهن وتلك الحالة الإدراكية تصدق على الأشياء الحاصلة في وهي الذهن صدقا عرضيا. العقل: العقل مرادف للنفس الناطقة هو جوهر مجرد في ذاته لا في فعله والعقل الذي هو مرادف الملك جوهر مجرد في ذاته وفعله كليهما، وقد يطلق العقل على القوة المدركة. لم يتعرض جواب عما يقال: إن المصنف عليه قسم العلم إلى قسمين قبل تعريفه وهو باطل، والجواب إما لكفاية التصور بوجه ما يعني أن المراد ببطلان التقسيم قبل التعريف أن تقسيم الشيء قبل معرفته بوجه ما باطل، وهو لم يلزم ههنا؛ لأن العلم معلوم الأذهان بوجه ما وإما لأن تعريف العلم إلخ. (عبد) قيل: القائل الإمام الرازي وجه الضعف أن كون العلم بديهيا لا يستلزم أن لا ينبه عليه في مقام التقسيم، فإن أيضا قد يكون خفيا، فلابد لإزالة الخفاء وتعيين المقسم من التنبيه عليه. البديهي اعتقادا: اعلم أن اعتقاد النسبة إما بحيث يبقى احتمال الغير، فالغالب ظن والمغلوب وهم وشك إن تساويا، وإما لم يبق فجزم فجهل مركب إن لم يطابق الواقع، وإن طابقه فتقليد إن زال بتشكيك المشكك، وإن لم يزل فيقين، فالوهم والشك من التصورات والبواقي من التصديقات. (إسماعيل بزيادة) اختار يعني لما جعل التصديق نفس الإذعان، فقد اختار مذهب الحكماء من القدماء، قال السيد السند قدس سره الشريف في حواشيه على شرح الشمسية: هذا هو الحق. (عبد) بيان التصديق والتصوّر وإلا فتصور. والحكم دون المجموع المركب منه ومن تصور الطرفين كما زعمه الإمام الرازي. واختار مذهب القدماء حيث جعل متعلق الإذعان والحكم الذي هو جزء أخير للقضية هو النسبة الخبرية الثبوتية أو السلبية لا وقوع النسبة الثبوتية التقييدية أو لا وقوعها؛ إذ المصنف سيشير إلى تثليث أجزاء القضية في مباحث القضايا قوله وإلا فتصور : سواء كان إدراكا لأمر واحد، كتصور زيد الطرفين وفيه نظر : فإن التصديق عند الإمام مركب من التصورات الثلاثة ،والحكم فلا بد من ذكر النسبة، كما لا يخفى، إلا أن يقال: إنه ترك اعتمادا على القريحة السليمة أو أن المراد من الطرفين حال كون النسبة رابطة بينهما . ( إسماعيل) زعمه أشار بقوله: "زعم" إلى ضعف مذهب الإمام، ووجهه على ما قاله السيد السند قدس سره الشريف: إن كلا من التصور والتصديق ممتاز عن الآخر بطريق خاص؛ ليحصل ،به، فلابد في تقسيم العلم ملاحظة ذلك الامتياز، وتلك الملاحظة مرئية على طور تقسيمهم دون تقسيمه. (إسماعيل) النسبة ولو قال نسبة الاتصال أو اللاتصال أو نسبة الانفصال أو اللانفصال لما خرج التصديقات الشرطية. :أقول لما كان أصل الشرطية هو الحملية بازدياد أدوات الاتصال والانفصال فقوله: النسبة الخبرية الثبوتية أو السلبية شامل للشرطيات أيضًا. (محشي) من "زيد لا وقوع يعني ما جعل متعلق الإذعان وقوع النسبة إلخ، كما هو عند المتأخرين واعلم أن الحكماء قاطبة بعد اتفاقهم على أن التصديق بسيط؛ إذ هو عبارة عن الإذعان والحكم اختلفوا في أن متعلق الإذعان إما النسبة الخبرية الثبوتية أو السلبية أو وقوع النسبة التقييدية أو لا وقوعها، فاختار المتقدمون منهم الأول، وقالوا بتثليث أجزاء القضية : المحكوم عليه والمحكوم به والنسبة الخبرية الثبوتية والسلبية وهذا هو الحق؛ إذ لا يفهم من قائم مثلا إلا نسبة واحدة، ولا يحتاج في عقده إلى نسبة أخرى، والتصديق عندهم نوع آخر من الإدراك، مغاير للتصور مغايرة ذاتية لا باعتبار المتعلق، وذهب المتأخرون منهم إلى الثاني وقالوا بتربيع أجزاء القضية: المحكوم عليه والمحكوم به والنسبة التقييدية ثبوتية كانت أو سلبية سموها بالنسبة الحكمية التي هي مورد الحكم بمعنى النسبة التامة الخبرية والرابع نسبة خبرية هي وقوعها ولا وقوعها إلا أن يقال ليس مقصودهم إثبات النسبتين المتغايرتين بالذات. (عبد) سيشير حيث قال في بحث القضايا يسمى المحكوم عليه موضوعا والمحكوم به محمولا والدال على النسبة رابطة. سواء كان وقوع النفي على مجموع قوله : "إذعانا للنسبة" بحيث ينحصر أقسام التصور أيضا.
If it is an assent to the relation, then it is tasdiq. The definition of knowledge: the form obtained from a thing in the mind? And the author did not address its definition; either because of sufficiency with a certain aspect of tasawwur in the context of division, or because the definition of knowledge is well-known and widespread, or because knowledge is self-evident in conception as has been said. His saying: 'If it is an assent to the relation' means a belief in the predicative relational proposition, affirmative like assenting that Zayd is standing, or negative like the belief that he is not standing. For he chose the position of the philosophers who made tasdiq the same as assent. The obtained form: that knowledge is the form arising and abstracted from it, whether it has it or not. And he turned away from the definition, i.e., the well-known one, which is the obtaining of the form of a thing in the mind; because what is divided into tasawwur and tasdiq is the earning and acquired knowledge, as is apparent from consideration of the purpose of this art, and 'obtaining' has no role in earning, even though obtaining is not a real meaning of knowledge. How so? Knowledge is disclosure, and we know intuitively that when the form obtains in itself, disclosure obtains and there is no need to extract the meaning of obtaining from it. This is what the clear view indicates. As for the precise view, it rules that what is meant by 'obtaining the form' is the meaning obtained via the infinitive, and its reality is what is expressed in Persian as 'danash' (knowledge), a cognitive state realized when the thing obtains in the mind, and that cognitive state is predicated of things obtaining in the mind accidentally. The intellect: 'aql is synonymous with the rational soul; it is a substance abstract in essence but not in action, and the intellect that is synonymous with 'king' is a substance abstract in both essence and action. The intellect is also applied to the perceptive power. He did not address a response to what is said: that the author divided knowledge into two parts before defining it, which is invalid. The response is either sufficiency with a certain aspect of tasawwur? meaning that what is meant by the invalidity of division before definition is that dividing something before knowing it in some respect is invalid, and it does not apply here because knowledge is known to minds in some respect, or because the definition of knowledge, etc. (Abd) It was said: the speaker is Imam al-Razi: the point of weakness is that knowledge being self-evident does not entail that one should not alert to it in the context of division, for it may also be obscure. So to remove obscurity and determine the divided thing, alerting to it is necessary. The self-evident in belief: Know that belief in a relation either leaves room for other possibility, then the predominant is suspicion, the overwhelmed is delusion, and doubt if they are equal; or it leaves no room, then it is categorical, then it is compound ignorance if it does not correspond to reality; if it corresponds, then it is imitation if it disappears with the doubt of a doubter, and if it does not disappear, it is certainty. His saying 'Otherwise, it is tasawwur' whether it is an apprehension of a single thing, like the conception of Zayd. (The two extremes) and there is a consideration: for tasdiq according to the Imam is composed of three conceptions and the judgment, so the relation must be mentioned, as is obvious, unless it is said that he omitted it relying on the sound nature, or that what is meant by 'the two extremes' is with the relation connecting them. (Ismail) His saying 'claimed' indicates the weakness of the Imam's position. Its explanation as Sayyid al-Sind said: each of tasawwur and tasdiq is distinct from the other by a specific path, so in the division of knowledge, that distinction must be observed, and that observation is visible in their manner of division but not in his division. (Ismail) The relation: if he had said 'relation of conjunction or non-conjunction' or 'relation of disjunction or non-disjunction', the conditional tasdiqat would not have been excluded. I say: since the origin of the conditional is the categorical with the addition of tools of conjunction and disjunction, his saying 'the affirmative or negative predicative relation' includes the conditionals as well. (Muhashi) From 'Zayd'? 'Non-occurrence' means what he made the object of assent is the occurrence of the relation, etc., as is the case with the later scholars. Know that all the philosophers after agreeing that tasdiq is simple, for it is assent and judgment, differed over whether the object of assent is the affirmative or negative predicative relation or the occurrence or non-occurrence of the attributive relation. The ancients chose the first and said with tripartite division of the proposition: the subject, the predicate, and the affirmative or negative predicative relation. And this is the truth, for from 'standing' for example, only one relation is understood, and it does not need another relation for its connection. And tasdiq according to them is another type of apprehension, different from tasawwur by essential difference, not by consideration of the object. The later scholars went to the second and said with quadripartite division of the proposition: the subject, the predicate, the attributive relation (whether affirmative or negative) which they call the judgmental relation that is the locus of judgment in the sense of the complete predicative relation, and the fourth is a predicative relation which is its occurrence or non-occurrence. Unless it is said that they did not intend to prove two essentially different relations. (Abd) He will later refer when he says in the discussion of propositions: the subject is called the subject, the predicate is called the predicate, and the indicator of the relation is the copula. Whether the negation applies to the whole of his saying 'assent to the relation' such that the divisions of tasawwur are also restricted.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening of a text on logic, likely Tahzeeb al-Mantiq. It addresses the definition of knowledge ('ilm) and its division into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). The commentator explains that if knowledge involves assenting to a relation (nisba) in a proposition, it is tasdiq; otherwise, it is tasawwur. He notes that the author did not explicitly define 'ilm, giving three possible reasons: either because tasawwur is sufficient for the purpose of division, or because the definition is well-known, or because knowledge is self-evident. The commentator then discusses the nature of tasdiq, siding with the ancient philosophers (hukama') who consider tasdiq to be the act of assenting (idh'an) to the predicative relation, whether affirmative or negative. He contrasts this with the view of Imam al-Razi, who considered tasdiq to include the entire proposition (subject, predicate, and judgment). The commentator argues that tasdiq is simple, not composite, and that the judgment is only the relation, not the entire proposition. The passage also delves into the division of propositions: the ancients held a tripartite structure (subject, predicate, relation), while the later scholars added a fourth element (the occurrence or non-occurrence of the attributive relation). The commentator favors the tripartite view, stating that only one relation is needed. The discussion includes clarifications on terms like 'aql (intellect) and the various types of belief (certainty, doubt, etc.). The parenthetical names (Abd, Ismail, Muhashi) are likely marginal glosses or commentary references.

How many parts does the ancient philosophers' view of a proposition include?
A) Two parts: subject and predicate

What Is Mantiq?

Dissecting the Definition of Nazar
Author defines speculation (nazar) and justifies the choice of definition over the famous one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the genus and differentia in the definition of nazar and classify the definition as hadd or rasm.

Core Idea
Nazar is the soul's direction toward known matters to reach the unknown.

The author introduces a definition of nazar that is not the most famous one. Let's break it down into its logical components to understand its structure and why it was chosen.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined in the Arabic. It is 'النظر' (al-nazar).
The definition is introduced by 'وهو ملاحظة المعقول لتحصيل المجهول'.
2
Extract the genus
What broader category does the author place nazar in? The sharh explains it as 'توجه النفس نحو الأمر المعلوم' (the soul's direction toward the known matter). This direction is the genus.
In logical terms, the genus is the general action or process of directing.
3
Extract the differentia
What distinguishes nazar from other forms of direction? It is 'لتحصيل أمر غير معلوم' (to obtain an unknown matter). This purpose is the differentia.
The differentia specifies that the direction is goal-oriented towards acquiring new knowledge.
4
Compare with the famous definition
The famous definition is 'ترتيب أمور معلومة للتأدي إلى مجهول' (arrangement of known matters leading to an unknown). Compare this with the author's: the author uses 'ملاحظة' (contemplation) instead of 'ترتيب' and does not require composition.
The author's definition is broader, including simple concepts and conjectural matters.
5
Determine the definition type
Is this a complete definition (hadd haqiqi) or a description (rasm)? Since it gives genus and differentia, it is a hadd haqiqi. The author's inclusion of even conjecture shows it covers all instances.
A hadd haqiqi must include all instances and exclude all non-instances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريف النظر: وهو ملاحظة المعقول لتحصيل المجهول. قوله: وهو ملاحظة المعقول: أي النظر، توجه النفس نحو الأمر المعلوم لتحصيل أمر غير معلوم. إنما عدل عن التعريف المشهور، وهو ترتيب أمور معلومة للتأدي إلى مجهول؛ ليشمل جميع أفراد النظر بلا كلفة سواء كان بالمفرد أو بالمركب معلوما كان أو مظنونا أو مجهولا بالجهل المركب. وإنما كان الاستدلال تجشما؛ لأن المستدل صار هدفا لسهام المنوع والمعارضات، سيما في هذا الزمان الذي جعل النظر فيه للمكابرة والضاد المجادلة والفساد، وصارت المناظرة مطروحة النظر وقبيحة المنظر، فطوبى لمن سلك مسلك النقل والحكاية، وهو أحق أن يوصف بالدراية.
The definition of speculation: It is the contemplation of the intellectible to obtain the unknown. His statement: 'It is the contemplation of the intellectible' means speculation, the soul's direction toward the known matter to obtain an unknown matter. He only deviated from the famous definition – which is the arrangement of known matters leading to an unknown – to include all individuals of speculation without difficulty, whether by simple or composite, whether known, conjectured, or unknown by compound ignorance. Inference is only burdensome because the inferrer becomes a target for the arrows of the preventer and objections, especially in this time in which speculation is made for obstinacy, enmity, argumentation, and corruption, and debate has become contemptible in its gaze and ugly in its appearance. Blessed is the one who follows the path of transmission and narration, and he is more worthy to be described as knowledgeable.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage defines the key term nazar (speculation, reasoning). The matn gives the definition: 'contemplation of the intellectible to obtain the unknown.' The sharh explains that nazar is the soul's direction (tawajjuh) towards a known matter in order to obtain an unknown matter. The commentator notes that this definition is a departure from the more famous definition of nazar as 'arrangement of known matters leading to an unknown.' The reason for the departure is to be more inclusive: this definition covers speculation that uses simple terms (mufrad) as well as composite (murakkab), and it includes cases where the starting point is known, conjectured (maznun), or even ignorance (compound ignorance). The text then explains why inference (istidlal) is burdensome: the one who infers becomes vulnerable to objections and opposition, especially in a time when speculation is used for contentious debate rather than truth. Therefore, the commentator praises the path of transmission (naql) and narration (hikaya) as more praiseworthy. This reflects a pedagogical concern that reasoning must be done properly to avoid fallacies, and that reliance on transmitted knowledge can be safer in corrupt times.

Key Takeaway
Nazar is defined as the soul's direction toward known matters to obtain the unknown, a definition that is broader than the famous one and covers all forms of reasoning.

Why the Author Deviated from the Famous Definition
Author defines speculation (nazar) and justifies the choice of definition over the famous one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the author chose the alternative definition of nazar and identify the dangers of inference he warns against.

Core Idea
The author's definition is more inclusive and avoids the burden of the famous definition.

The author deliberately departs from the well-known definition of nazar. Why? And what does he say about the difficulties of inference? This lesson unpacks his reasoning and the cautionary note about the times.

Guided Path
1
Recall the famous definition
The famous definition of nazar is 'ترتيب أمور معلومة للتأدي إلى مجهول' (arrangement of known matters leading to an unknown). Note that it emphasizes ordered steps.
This definition is common in earlier logic texts.
2
Identify the author's alternative
The author defines nazar as 'ملاحظة المعقول لتحصيل المجهول' (contemplation of the intellectible to obtain the unknown). He replaces 'arrangement' with 'contemplation' and drops the requirement of composite steps.
The author uses 'ملاحظة' which is a broader term than 'ترتيب'.
3
Understand the reason for deviation
The author says 'إنما عدل عن التعريف المشهور ... ليشمل جميع أفراد النظر بلا كلفة' – He deviated to include all individuals of speculation without difficulty. This includes simple concepts and conjectural matters.
The inclusive definition avoids the limitation that speculation must be composite.
4
Recognize the burden of inference
The passage then states that inference (istidlal) is burdensome because the inferrer becomes a target for objections. This reflects the challenging nature of rational debate.
The commentator laments that speculation is often used for obstinacy and corruption.
5
Assess the alternative: transmission
The passage concludes by praising the path of transmission (naql) and narration, suggesting that in corrupt times, relying on transmitted knowledge is safer and more praiseworthy.
This is a practical pedagogical note about the use of reason versus authority.

The Definition of Nazar: Observation of the Intelligible
Author defines nazar and explains the choice of each term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three components of the definition of nazar and explain why each term was chosen.

Core Idea
Nazar is the soul's active direction toward the known to acquire the unknown.

In this passage, the author defines nazar, the cornerstone of logic. He offers a definition that is broader than the famous one, encompassing both simple and compound, certain and conjectural. Let's analyze its components and the rationale for each word choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Find the Arabic sentence that defines nazar: 'وهو ملاحظة المعقول لتحصيل المجهول'. This is the core definition.
The definition is compact and deliberate.
2
Break down the components
The definition has three parts: ملاحظة (observation), المعقول (the intelligible), لتحصيل المجهول (to acquire the unknown). Note that each term is deliberately chosen over alternatives.
The author explains why he chose each word.
3
Understand 'observation'
The author chose ملاحظة over حصول because observation implies active direction of the soul. Without active direction, it is not nazar even if knowledge is present.
This distinguishes nazar from mere passive acquisition.
4
Understand 'intelligible' vs 'known'
The author uses معقول (intelligible) instead of معلوم (known) to emphasize that nazar deals with universal mental content, and for rhetorical harmony (saj').
This also narrows the scope to concepts, not external objects.
5
Understand 'unknown' as relative
The unknown (المجهول) is not absolute; it is unknown only in the specific aspect sought. Seeking the absolutely unknown is impossible, and seeking the already known is redundant.
This avoids the objection that nazar cannot aim at something completely unknown.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة وهو ملاحظة المعقول؛ لتحصيل المجهول. تعريف النظر إلى تجشم الاستدلال كما ارتكبه القوم، وذلك؛ لأنا إذا رجعنا إلى وجداننا وجدنا من التصورات ما هو حاصل لنا بلا نظر كتصور الحرارة والبرودة ومنها ما هو حاصل بالنظر والفكر كتصور حقيقة الملك والجن، وكذا من التصديقات ما يحصل بلا نظر كالتصديق بأن الشمس مشرقة والنار محرقة، ومنها ما يحصل بالنظر كالتصديق بأن العالم حادث والصانع موجود. قوله: وهو ملاحظة المعقول: أي النظر، توجه النفس نحو الأمر المعلوم لتحصيل أمر غير معلوم. إنما عدل عن التعريف المشهور وهو ترتيب أمور معلومة للتأدي إلى مجهول؛ ليشمل جميع أفراد النظر بلا كلفة سواء كان بالمفرد أو بالمركب معلوما كان أو مظنونا أو مجهولا بالجهل المركب. (محشي) لأنا إذا رجعنا لإزالة الخفاء وإشارة إلى أن هذا الوجدان عام لا خاص فلا يرد أن الوجدان لا يصير دليلا على الغير. (عبد الملك) هي جوهر مجرد في ذاته وفي فعله أو جسم نوراني يتشكل بأشكال مختلفة لا يذكر ولا يؤنث. (تحفه) والجن: أي حقيقته وهي جسم ناري يتشكل بأشكال مختلفة يذكر ويؤنث. والصانع موجود لأن الصانع مؤثر في المصنوع الموجود وكل مؤثر في المصنوع الموجود موجود فالصانع موجود؛ لأن المصنوع موجود ممكن ولابد للموجود الممكن من موجد موجود يرجح أحد طرفيه وهو الصانع. (عبد) ملاحظة: وإنما قال الملاحظة ولم يقل حصول المعقول أو العلم بالشيء؛ لأن حصول المعقول والعلم به قد يتحقق بدون التوجه والالتفات وحينئذ لم يتحقق النظر والاكتساب. (شوستري) المعلوم: الذي حصل صورته في العقل، فلا يخفى أنه لو قال نحو الأمر المعقول لكان أنسب بعبارة المتن وأوفق؛ لما سيذكره من وجه العدول عن لفظ المعلوم إلى لفظ المعقول. (عبد) غير معلوم بالوجه الذي يطلب لا من جميع الوجوه؛ لأن طلب المجهول المطلق محال بالضرورة، وإنما اعتبر الجهل في المطلوب؛ لاستحالة استعلام المعلوم؛ لأنه تحصيل الحاصل. (عبد)
The introduction: And it (nazar) is observation of the intelligible to acquire the unknown. [Then] Definition of nazar: [It involves] enduring the hardship of inference as the people undertook it. That is because if we return to our intuition, we find among concepts some that are present to us without nazar, like the concept of heat and cold, and among them some that are present through nazar and reflection, like the concept of the reality of angels and jinn. Similarly, among assents, some are obtained without nazar, like the assent that the sun is rising and fire is burning, and among them some are obtained through nazar, like the assent that the world is temporally originated and the Creator exists. His statement: 'And it is observation of the intelligible' means nazar is the soul's direction towards the known thing to acquire an unknown thing. He deviated from the famous definition, which is the arrangement of known things to arrive at an unknown, in order to include all individuals of nazar without hardship, whether simple or compound, known or conjectured or unknown with composite ignorance. (Commentary) 'Because if we return' is to remove obscurity and a sign that this intuition is general not specific, so it is not objected that intuition does not become evidence for another. (Abd al-Malik) It (angel) is a pure substance in essence and act or a luminous body that takes different forms, not masculine or feminine. (Tuhfah) And jinn: its reality is a fiery body that takes different forms, masculine and feminine. And the Creator exists because the Creator is effective in the existing artifact, and every effective in the existing artifact exists, so the Creator exists; because the artifact is an existing possible, and the existing possible must have an existing efficient that preponderates one of its two sides, and that is the Creator. (Abd) Observation: He said observation and did not say acquisition of the intelligible or knowledge of the thing, because acquisition of the intelligible and knowledge of it may occur without direction and attention, and then nazar and acquisition would not occur. (Shustari) The known: that which its form has been obtained in the intellect. It is not hidden that if he said 'the intelligible thing' it would be more appropriate to the text and more in harmony with what he will mention regarding the reason for deviating from the word known to the word intelligible. (Abd) Unknown in the aspect sought, not from all aspects, because seeking the absolute unknown is impossible by necessity, and ignorance in the sought is considered only because it is impossible to know the known because it is the acquisition of the already acquired. (Abd)
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage defines 'nazar' (theoretical contemplation) as the observation of the intelligible to acquire the unknown. The author first states the definition, then explains why he deviated from the famous definition (arranging known things to reach an unknown). The reason is to cover all types of nazar without unnecessary restriction: whether the object is simple or compound, known, conjectured, or even unknown with composite ignorance. He supports the definition by referring to intuition: we have concepts and assents that are immediate (like heat or sun rising) and others that require thought (like reality of angels or evidence for a creator). The commentary expands on the definition, explaining that 'observation' implies active direction of the soul, not mere presence of knowledge. The examples of angels and jinn illustrate the kind of things known through nazar. The discussion of the creator uses a syllogism: the artifact exists, every existing possible needs an existing efficient cause, therefore the creator exists. The passage also addresses why 'observation of the intelligible' was chosen over other terms: to include both simple and compound, to emphasize that nazar applies to certain and conjectural knowledge, and for rhetorical harmony (saj'). The commentary clarifies that the 'unknown' is not absolutely unknown but unknown in the particular aspect sought.

Key Terms
النظر
ملاحظة
المعقول
المجهول
الوجدان
التجشم

Checkpoint
Which word in the definition of nazar emphasizes the active direction of the soul?
A) ملاحظة
B) المعقول
C) المجهول
D) تحصيل

Key Takeaway
The definition of nazar is deliberately broad to include all types of contemplation, and each term is chosen for a specific reason: observation implies active direction, intelligible restricts to mental content, and unknown is relative.

The Rationale for the Definition and an Illustrative Syllogism
Author gives example of proving Creator's existence as an instance of nazar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the syllogism proving the existence of the Creator and explain how it illustrates the definition of nazar.

Core Idea
The syllogism about the Creator shows nazar in action: from known premises to an unknown conclusion.

The author not only defines nazar but also gives examples to justify his definition. A key example is the proof that the Creator exists. This example demonstrates how nazar works as observation of the intelligible to acquire the unknown.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conclusion
The conclusion is 'الصانع موجود' (the Creator exists). This is the unknown (المجهول) being acquired.
The conclusion is stated directly in the passage.
2
Identify the known premises
The premises are: 1) The artifact (المصنوع) is an existing possible. 2) Every existing possible must have an existing efficient cause that preponderates one of its two sides.
These are the 'known things' from which the inference starts.
3
Reconstruct the syllogism
Formally: All existing possibles (M) have an existing efficient cause (P). The world (S) is an existing possible (M). Therefore, the world has an existing efficient cause, i.e., the Creator exists (S is P).
This is a categorical syllogism in the first figure (Barbara).
4
Note the terms
The intelligible (المعقول) here are the universal concepts: possible, necessary, cause, effect. The observation (ملاحظة) is the act of linking these concepts.
The soul actively 'observes' the logical connection.
5
See how this fits the definition
The soul directs from known things (premises) to an unknown (conclusion). The premises are 'intelligibles' (universal propositions), and the conclusion is 'acquired'. This perfectly exemplifies nazar.
The example shows that nazar is not restricted to simple apprehension but includes inferential reasoning.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The introduction: And it (nazar) is observation of the intelligible to acquire the unknown. [Then] Definition of nazar: [It involves] enduring the hardship of inference as the people undertook it. That is because if we return to our intuition, we find among concepts some that are present to us without nazar, like the concept of heat and cold, and among them some that are present through nazar and reflection, like the concept of the reality of angels and jinn. (Abd al-Malik) It (angel) is a pure substance in essence and act or a luminous body that takes different forms, not masculine or feminine. (Tuhfah) And jinn: its reality is a fiery body that takes different forms, masculine and feminine. And the Creator exists because the Creator is effective in the existing artifact, and every effective in the existing artifact exists, so the Creator exists; because the artifact is an existing possible, and the existing possible must have an existing efficient that preponderates one of its two sides, and that is the Creator. (Abd) Observation: He said observation and did not say acquisition of the intelligible or knowledge of the thing, because acquisition of the intelligible and knowledge of it may occur without direction and attention, and then nazar and acquisition would not occur. (Shustari) The known: that which its form has been obtained in the intellect. It is not hidden that if he said 'the intelligible thing' it would be more appropriate to the text and more in harmony with what he will mention regarding the reason for deviating from the word known to the word intelligible. (Abd) Unknown in the aspect sought, not from all aspects, because seeking the absolute unknown is impossible by necessity, and ignorance in the sought is considered only because it is impossible to know the known because it is the acquisition of the already acquired. (Abd)
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage defines 'nazar' (theoretical contemplation) as the observation of the intelligible to acquire the unknown. The author first states the definition, then explains why he deviated from the famous definition (arranging known things to reach an unknown). The reason is to cover all types of nazar without unnecessary restriction: whether the object is simple or compound, known, conjectured, or even unknown with composite ignorance. He supports the definition by referring to intuition: we have concepts and assents that are immediate (like heat or sun rising) and others that require thought (like reality of angels or evidence for a creator). The commentary expands on the definition, explaining that 'observation' implies active direction of the soul, not mere presence of knowledge. The examples of angels and jinn illustrate the kind of things known through nazar. The discussion of the creator uses a syllogism: the artifact exists, every existing possible needs an existing efficient cause, therefore the creator exists. The passage also addresses why 'observation of the intelligible' was chosen over other terms: to include both simple and compound, to emphasize that nazar applies to certain and conjectural knowledge, and for rhetorical harmony (saj'). The commentary clarifies that the 'unknown' is not absolutely unknown but unknown in the particular aspect sought.

Why 'Ma'qūl' is Preferred Over 'Ma'lūm' in Defining Logic
Commentator lists three benefits of choosing 'ma'qūl' over 'ma'lūm' in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three benefits of using 'ma'qūl' over 'ma'lūm' in the definition of logic and explain how each benefit serves terminological precision.

Core Idea
Choosing 'ma'qūl' avoids ambiguity, signals universality, and even observes rhyme – precision in definition is no accident.

The commentator takes a moment to explain why the matn author chose the term 'ma'qūl' (intelligible) rather than 'ma'lūm' (known) in defining logic. At first glance, this may seem like a minor stylistic choice. However, as the commentary shows, the shift serves three distinct purposes: avoiding a homonym, clarifying the subject matter of logic (universals), and maintaining textual harmony. Understanding this reasoning sharpens our appreciation for the careful craft of the classical scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms being compared.
Locate 'ma'lūm' and 'ma'qūl' in the Arabic. Note that the commentator explicitly contrasts them, stating 'al-ʿudūl ʿan lafẓ al-maʿlūm ilā al-maʿqūl' (turning away from the term 'maʿlūm' to 'maʿqūl').
2
Understand the problem with 'ma'lūm'.
Why is 'ma'lūm' problematic? The commentator says it is a 'lafẓ mushtarak' (homonym). A homonym has multiple meanings, which causes confusion in a definition. Definitions must be clear and unambiguous.
Examples of homonyms in Arabic: 'ʿayn' can mean eye, spring, or spy. Using such a term in a definition would be avoided.
3
Extract the second benefit: signaling universality.
'Ma'qūl' points to 'maʿqūlāt' (intelligibles), which are universal concepts (kulliyāt) in the mind, as opposed to particulars (juzʾiyyāt) perceived by the senses. This clarifies that logic deals with universals, not particulars.
The commentator adds that the particular is neither 'kāsiban' (acquisitive) nor 'muktasaban' (acquired), meaning it plays no role in the acquisition of knowledge.
4
Note the third benefit: rhyme.
The commentator mentions 'riʿāyat al-sajʿ' (observing rhyme). This shows that classical scholars valued literary elegance even in technical definitions, as it aids memorization and textual harmony.
Rhyme is often used in matn texts to make them easier to memorize.
5
Synthesize the overall lesson.
The three benefits illustrate that the choice of words in a definition is deliberate: it must be unambiguous, accurately delimit the subject matter, and be aesthetically pleasing or mnemonic. This is a hallmark of well-crafted classical texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي العدول عن لفظ المعلوم إلى المعقول فوائد منها : التحرز عن استعمال اللفظ المشترك في التعريف ومنها: التنبيه على أن الفكر إنما يجري في المعقولات أي الأمور الكلية الحاصلة في العقل دون الأمور الجزئية؛ فإن الجزئي لا يكون كاسبا ولا مكتسبا ومنها: رعاية السجع.
And in turning away from the term 'the known' (al-ma'lum) to 'the intelligible' (al-ma'qul) there are benefits: among them, avoiding the use of a homonym (al-lafz al-mushtarak) in definition; among them, alerting that thought only proceeds in intelligibles (al-ma'qulat), i.e., universal matters present in the mind, not particular matters; for the particular is neither acquisitive nor acquired; and among them, observing rhyme (al-saj').
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage explains why the author of the matn chose the word 'ma'qūl' (intelligible) instead of 'ma'lūm' (known) in defining logic. The commentator, likely al-Tahzeeb's commentator, lists three reasons. First, avoiding lexical ambiguity: the word 'ma'lūm' is mushtarak (homonym) with multiple meanings, while 'ma'qūl' is more precise. Second, signaling that thought (fikr) deals with universals (kulliyāt) not particulars (juz'iyyāt), because particulars are perceived by sense, not reason, and cannot be used to acquire new knowledge. Third, for the sake of rhyme (saj') in the text. The commentary thus highlights the deliberate precision in terminology.

Logic as a Canon and Its Subject Matter
The author defines logic as a canon and identifies its subject as the study of essential accidents of mental beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of logic as a 'qanun' and explain its subject matter as the study of essential accidents of mental beings.

Core Idea
Logic is a canon that guards the mind from error, studying essential accidents of concepts.

This passage from the introduction of a classic logic textbook sets out the precise definition of logic: a canon (qanun) that protects the mind from error. It also clarifies what logic studies — not the external world, but mental beings and their essential accidents. Understanding this double definition is the foundation for the entire logical tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of logic
Locate the sentence stating: 'قانون يعصم مراعاته الذهن عن الخطأ في الفكر'. Break it down: logic is a 'qanun' (canon), and its observance ('mura'atuhu') guards the mind from error in thought.
This definition is a rasm (description) because it mentions a distinguishing effect, not the essence.
2
Understand 'qanun' as a technical term
The passage explains 'qanun' as a universal proposition from which particular rulings are derived, giving the grammar example: 'Every agent is nominative'. This shows how a canon functions as a general rule.
The term originates from Greek or Syriac, originally meaning 'ruler' (straight line).
3
Grasp the subject matter (mawdu')
The text defines the subject of a science as that which is investigated regarding its essential accidents. For logic, the subject is mental beings (concepts and propositions), and its essential accidents include truth, falsity, validity, etc.
Essential accidents are attributes that necessarily follow the essence, like laughter for man.
4
Apply the example to see the method
The passage uses a syllogism: 'Zayd is an agent; every agent is nominative; therefore Zayd is nominative.' This illustrates how a universal canon (major premise) is applied to a particular via the first figure.
This shows the practical use of logic as a canon.

( إسماعيل) القانون أطلق "القانون" عليه أنه قوانين متعددة؛ تعبيرا عن الكل باسم الجزء، وفي ذلك إشارة إلى أن تلك

The introduction. Section on the definition of logic. To a canon that guards against error in thought, and that is logic, and its subject: And it is known from this [that] this definition of logic also: 'A canon whose observance guards the mind from error in thought.' So here two of the three things that the introduction was set to explain are known. The discussion remains on the third thing, which is to investigate what the subject of the science of logic is. So he pointed to it by his statement: 'And its subject, etc.' His statement: 'canon' — the word 'qanun' is Greek or Syriac, originally applied to the ruler of a book (straight line), and in technical term it is a universal proposition from which the rulings of its particular instances are known, such as the grammarians' statement: 'Every agent (fa'il) is nominative (marfu'),' for it is a universal ruling from which the states of particular agents are known. His statement: 'and its subject': the subject of a science is that which is investigated regarding its essential accidents, and the essential accident is that which occurs to the thing... And it has been known from this explanation that since the explanation of the need for logic was directed to defining it by its description (rasm) without conversion (because it is possible that it be defined by another characteristic besides the goal, which is 'isma), he began with explaining the need, then proceeded to divide knowledge into its two divisions up to the end of the introductions. So here: a rebuttal to what is imagined that the introduction was comprised of explaining the need, the drawing, and the subject. So why did the author leave the second? The rebuttal: that he did bring the explanation of the three things, but the first and third explicitly, and the second implicitly, and there is no harm; because it is more appropriate for the text. (Isma'il) The word 'qanun' is applied to it as multiple canons; expressing the whole by the name of a part, and in that is an indication that those canons, due to their sharing in one aspect which is regulation, are like one thing in the status of one canon (Shawshari). A universal proposition, likewise 'asl, 'qā'ida, and 'dābiṭa' are names for this proposition, and 'qanun' is used in the singular because of consideration of the individuals of that science... The way of knowledge is that the subject of this proposition, i.e., 'fa'il', is applied to the particular, e.g., 'Zayd' in 'Zayd beat', so it is said: 'Zayd is an agent', and this proposition resulting from applying the subject to the particular is made a minor premise of the first figure, and that proposition is made a major premise, such that it is said: 'Zayd is an agent and every agent is nominative', so the conclusion is 'Zayd is nominative'. Thus this method yields the ruling of Zayd, which is nominative. The subject of the science is only known as subject matter in general; because knowledge of the subject of logic depends on it; for the restricted cannot be known without knowledge of the absolute. What is meant by 'occurrence' is predicative (haml bi-l-muwāṭāt), i.e., essential predication. And the mention of attributes like 'laughter' and 'wonder' is by way of tolerance; the intended meaning is 'one who laughs' and 'one who wonders'. They are lenient lest the essence be understood; for it is not an accident but the very substrate. Isma'il with addition by 'Abd al-Nabi)
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage from the introduction defines logic and discusses its subject. It begins by noting that from the previous discussion, two of the three intended aims (the need for logic and its definition) have been explained, and now the third remains: the subject of logic. The author provides the definition of logic as 'a canon whose observance guards the mind from error in thought'. Then it explains the word 'qanun' (canon): it is a Greek or Syriac loanword originally meaning a ruler (for writing), and in technical terminology it means a universal proposition from which the rulings of particular instances are derived. An example is given from grammar: 'Every agent (fa'il) is nominative (marfu')', from which we know the state of particular agents. Next, the passage defines the subject of a science as 'that which is investigated regarding its essential accidents', and an essential accident is something that occurs to the thing. The commentary then clarifies why the author presented the need for logic first: because it leads to the definition by description (rasm) without needing the opposite (i.e., defining by another property). The structure of the introduction is defended: although it was supposed to cover three things (need, definition, subject), the definition was given implicitly. The commentary also glosses the word 'qanun' as used in the plural sense (multiple canons) but expressed in the singular to indicate they form a single system. Finally, it explains how universal propositions are applied to particulars using a syllogism in the first figure, using the grammatical example: 'Zayd is an agent' (minor) and 'Every agent is nominative' (major) yields 'Zayd is nominative'. The passage ends with a note on essential accidents: they are predicated essentially, and examples like laughter or wonder are tolerantly attributed to the substrate.

موضوع
عرض ذاتي

The Two Types of Essential Accident in Logic
Commentator defines logic and explains the concept of essential accident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between primary and coextensive essential accidents and identify which type applies in a given definition from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Essential accidents define subjects; without them, science loses its scope.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks the concept of essential accident (`arad dhati), which is crucial for defining the subject matter (mawdu`) of any science. You learn that essential accidents come in two types: those that belong to a thing primarily and essentially, and those that attach through a coextensive intermediary. This distinction is not mere terminology—it shapes how we define what a science studies.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of `arad dhati`
Find the Arabic phrase `العرض الذاتي` in the passage and note its definition: `ما يعرض الشيء إما أوّلاً وبالذات... أو بواسطة أمر مساوٍ لذلك الشيء`.
The definition is given as a disjunction (two cases).
2
Understand the first type (primary and essential)
The first type is `أوّلاً وبالذات`: the accident attaches to the thing simply because of what it is. The example is wonder (al-ta`ajjub) attaching to human insofar as he is human.
This means the accident naturally belongs to the subject without any intermediary.
3
Understand the second type (through a coextensive matter)
The second type is `بواسطة أمر مساوٍ`: the accident attaches through an intermediary that is coextensive (musawi) with the thing. The example is laughter: it actually belongs to the one who wonders (al-muta`ajjib), but is attributed to humans because humans are capable of wonder.
The intermediary (wasita) is a property that is equivalent to the subject in extension but not the same in essence.
4
Apply the distinction to a definition
Consider a definition of `insan` (human): `rational animal`. The capacity for logic (`nutq`) is a primary essential accident, while `being a writer` is not because it depends on culture—it would be through a coextensive intermediary if at all.
This skill helps in evaluating definitions in any Islamic science.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله :قانون القانون لفظ يوناني أو سرياني، موضوع في الأصل لمسطر الكتاب، وفي الاصطلاح قضية كلية يعرف منها أحكام جزئيات موضوعها، كقول النحاة كل فاعل مرفوع، فإنه حكم كلي يعرف منه أحوال جزئيات الفاعل. قوله: وموضوعه: موضوع العلم ما يبحث فيه عن عوارضه الذاتية، والعرض الذاتي: ما يعرض الشيء إما أوّلاً وبالذات كالتعجب اللاحق للإنسان من حيث أنه إنسان، وإما بواسطة أمر مساوٍ لذلك الشيء، كالضحك الذي يعرض حقيقة للمتعجب ثم ينسب عروضه إلى الإنسان بالعرض والمجاز. فافهم.
His statement: 'Law': 'Law' is a Greek or Syriac word, originally used for a ruler (straight edge) for writing, and in technical terminology it is a universal proposition from which rulings of its particular subjects are known, like the grammarians' statement: 'Every subject (fa'il) is marfu'[1]', for it is a universal ruling from which the states of particular subjects are known. His statement: 'and its subject matter': The subject matter of a science is that about which essential accidents are investigated, and the essential accident is that which occurs to a thing either primarily and essentially, like wonder (ta'ajjub) that attaches to the human being insofar as he is human, or through a matter coextensive with that thing, like laughter which actually occurs to the one who wonders (al-muta'ajjib) and then its occurrence is attributed to the human being metaphorically and figuratively. So understand.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of logic and its subject matter. The commentator begins by explaining the term 'law' (qanun), noting its origin and terminological meaning: a universal proposition that allows deriving rulings on its particulars, citing the grammatical example 'every subject is marfu'. The subject matter (mawdu') of a science is defined as that about which essential accidents are investigated. The essential accident ('arad dhati) is then defined and divided into two types: that which occurs to a thing primarily and essentially, such as wonder attaching to humans because they are human, and that which occurs through a coextensive matter, such as laughter occurring to the one who wonders (al-muta'ajjib) and then attributed to the human secondarily. The commentator emphasizes the need to differentiate between essential and accidental attributes, as this distinction is foundational in logic and the sciences.

Key Terms
قانون
موضوع
عرض ذاتي
واسطة في العروض

Checkpoint

C) Accidentally and without any reason

Key Takeaway
An essential accident is not just any attribute; it must attach either primarily and essentially or through a coextensive intermediary, a distinction that defines the subject matter of every science.

The Subject of Logic: Definitions and Arguments as Means to the Unknown
Commentary defines the subject of logic as knowledge that leads to unknown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a piece of conceptual or assent knowledge falls within the subject matter of logic based on the condition of leading to an unknown.

Core Idea
Logic studies knowledge only as a tool to reach the unknown, not knowledge for its own sake.

This passage from the commentary on the Tahdhib clarifies the exact scope of logic. Many beginners think logic studies all concepts and judgments, but the author narrows it down: logic only examines conceptual knowledge when it serves as a definition (mu'arraf) leading to an unknown concept, and assent knowledge when it serves as an argument (hujja) leading to an unknown judgment. This distinction is crucial for understanding why logic is a tool ('ala) for the sciences, not a science itself.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between conceptual and assent knowledge
Identify which type of knowledge is under discussion. Conceptual knowledge is a simple concept (e.g., 'man'), while assent knowledge is a judgment (e.g., 'the world is originated').
2
Identify the condition of leading (iysal)
Recognize that not all concepts or judgments are the subject of logic, only those that can lead to something unknown. For example, 'animal rational' leads to the concept of man; 'the world is changing, every changing is originated' leads to the assent that the world is originated.
3
Apply the condition to examples
Given a piece of knowledge, determine if it would be studied by a logician. For instance, knowledge of a particular person (Zayd) does not lead to a general concept, so it is outside logic.
4
Understand the implications for the scope of logic
Note that logic does not investigate knowledge as existing or as corresponding to reality; that is metaphysics. Logic's sole concern is the instrumental value of knowledge in acquiring new knowledge.

المقدمة ٣٣ مبحث موضوع المنطق المعلوم التصوري والتصديقي، من حيث أنه يوصل إلى مطلوب تصوري · • قوله: المعلوم التصوري: اعلم أن موضوع المنطق هو المعرّف والحجة. أما المعرف: فهو عبارة عن المعلوم التصوري، لكن لا مطلقا بل من حيث أنه يوصل إلى مجهول تصوري، كالحيوان الناطق الموصل إلى تصور الإنسان، وأما المعلوم التصوري الذي لا يوصل إلى مجهول تصوري، فلا معرّفا، والمنطقي لا يبحث عنه، كالأمور الجزئية المعلومة نحو: زيد وعمرو، وأما الحجة فهي عبارة عن المعلوم التصديقي، لكن لا مطلقا، أيضًا بل من حيث أنه يوصل إلى مطلوب تصديقي، كقولنا : العالم متغير وكل متغير حادث الموصل إلى التصديق بقولنا: العالم حادث، وأما مالا يوصل كقولنا النار حارة مثلا، فليس بحجة، والمنطقي لا ينظر فيه، بل يبحث عن المعرّف يسمى = أو إيماء إلى أن ذكر المبادي في هذا على سبيل المسامحة، والمراد منها المشتقات. ويمكن أن يكون إشعارا إلى أن المراد من نفي الواسطة في العرض الذاتي نفي الواسطة في العروض، وهي التي يكون ثبوت الوصف بالذات لها وبالعرض ،لذيها كالسفينة فإن الحركة ثابتة لها بالذات وللجالس بالعرض، لا نفي الواسطة في الثبوت، وهي التي تكون سببا وعلة لثبوت الصفة للموصوف، وتكون هذه الصفة ثابتة له باعتبار جعل الجاعل، وهو على قسمين: الأول: أن لا يكون الصفة ثابتة للواسطة أصلا، كالصباغ؛ فإنه واسطة وسبب لثبوت اللون للثوب، مع أنه ليس مصبوغاً وملوناً والثاني: أن يكون الواسطة أيضًا متصفة بالذات، فذو الواسطة والواسطة كلاهما متصفان بالذات، كاليد؛ فإنه واسطة في ثبوت الحركة للمفتاح، وهي ثابتة لكليهما بالذات.(إسماعيل بتغير واختصار) يوصل فموضوع المنطق هو المعلومات التصورية والتصديقية من حيث كونها موصلتين إلى مجهول، فلا يبحث فيه منها من حيث أنها موجودة أو غير موجودة جواهر أو أعراض، مطابقة لما في نفس الأمر أو غير مطابقة له؛ فإن البحث منها بهذه الحيثيات ليس من وظائف المنطق بل العلم الالهي. ثم اعلم أن هذا القيد -أي الإيصال- ليس علة لعروض العوارض وسببا له ولا دخل له في ذات المعروض أيضا كيف وعروض الجنسية والفصلية لمعروضهما ليس موقوفا على الإيصال كما لا يخفى فلا يرد أن الإيصال يبحث عنه في المنطق مع أنه من متممات موضوعه، وقد صرح أن موضوع الفن وما يتوقف عليه مفروغ عنه بالبحث في هذا الفن.
The introduction [page] 33. Section on the subject of logic: Conceptual and assent knowledge, insofar as it leads to a conceptual goal. · • His saying: 'conceptual knowledge': Know that the subject of logic is definition and argument. As for definition: it is conceptual knowledge, but not absolutely, rather insofar as it leads to an unknown concept, like animal rational leading to the concept of man. And as for conceptual knowledge that does not lead to an unknown concept, it is not a definition, and the logician does not investigate it, like known particular things such as Zayd and Amr. And as for argument: it is assent knowledge, but not absolutely, rather insofar as it leads to an assent goal, like our saying: the world is changing and every changing is originated, leading to the assent that the world is originated. And as for what does not lead, like our saying fire is hot for example, it is not an argument, and the logician does not consider it. Rather he investigates the definition called... = Or an indication that mentioning the principles here is by way of approximation, and what is meant by them are derivatives. And it can be a notification that what is meant by negating the intermediary in essential accident is negating the intermediary in occurrence, which is that the description subsists essentially for it and accidentally for its possessor, like the ship, for movement subsists essentially for it and accidentally for the passenger; not negating the intermediary in subsistence, which is a cause and reason for the subsistence of the attribute for the described, and this attribute subsists for it by virtue of the maker's making, and it is of two types: first, that the attribute does not subsist for the intermediary at all, like the dyer, for it is an intermediary and cause for the subsistence of color for the garment, while it is not dyed and colored; second, that the intermediary also is essentially qualified, so both the possessor of the intermediary and the intermediary are essentially qualified, like the hand, for it is an intermediary in the subsistence of movement for the key, and it subsists for both essentially. (Ismail with change and abbreviation) It leads: So the subject of logic is conceptual and assent information insofar as they lead to an unknown, so it does not investigate them insofar as they exist or not, substances or accidents, corresponding to reality or not; for investigation into these respects is not from the functions of logic but from divine science. Then know that this condition – i.e., leading – is not a cause for the occurrence of accidents nor a reason for it, nor does it have any role in the essence of the subject either. How could it, when the occurrence of genus and differentia for their subjects is not dependent on leading, as is not hidden. So it is not objectionable that leading is investigated in logic while it is from the complements of its subject, and it has been stated that the subject of the art and what depends on it is assumed to be done with by investigation in this art.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a definitional commentary on the subject matter (mawdu') of logic. It begins by stating that the subject of logic is conceptual and assent knowledge, but only under the condition that it leads to an unknown (majhul). The author distinguishes between two types of knowledge: conceptual (tasawwuri) and assent (tasdiqi). For conceptual knowledge, when it leads to an unknown concept, it is called a definition (mu'arraf); when it does not, like knowledge of particulars (Zayd, Amr), it is not investigated by the logician. For assent knowledge, when it leads to an unknown assent, it is called an argument (hujja); when it does not, like the statement 'fire is hot', it is not a concern of logic. The commentary then explains that the condition of 'leading' (iysal) is crucial: logic does not study knowledge in itself, but only as a means to something unknown. The author also addresses a subtle point: the negating of intermediary in essential accident refers to negating the intermediary in occurrence, not in subsistence. Examples from the previous page are recalled. The commentary then emphasizes that the subject of logic is conceptual and assent information only under this condition, and that logic does not investigate things as existing, as substances/accidents, or as corresponding to reality; those are the domain of metaphysics (al-ilm al-ilahi). Finally, the author argues that the condition of leading is not a cause for the accidents themselves, nor does it affect the essence of the subject; it is simply a condition for something to fall under the purview of logic. This clarification prevents a potential objection that logic studies leading while it is a complement of its subject.

Key Takeaway
Logic's subject is limited to conceptual and assent knowledge that functions as a means to uncover something previously unknown, excluding bare facts and particular instances.

What Is Mantiq?

The Three Types of Verbal Signification
Author defines three types of verbal signification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which type of verbal signification (muṭābaqa, taḍammun, or iltizām) a given word-meaning relationship exemplifies.

Core Idea
A word can signify its whole, a part, or something external.

When we hear a word, it evokes a meaning. But does it evoke the entire meaning, only a part, or something associated? The logicians classify this into three precise types. In this lesson, we explore these divisions and see how they apply to Islamic texts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of signification (dalāla)
Signification is the relationship between a word and its meaning. The author divides it into three based on what part of the meaning is signified.
These are standard across Islamic logic.
2
Identify muṭābaqa (congruence)
When a word signifies its entire meaning, it is muṭābaqa. For example, the word 'man' (insān) signifies the whole concept of rational animal.
This is the primary signification.
3
Identify taḍammun (inclusion)
When a word signifies a part of its meaning, it is taḍammun. For example, 'man' implies 'animal' because animal is part of its definition.
The part is contained in the whole.
4
Identify iltizām (commitment)
When a word signifies something external to its meaning but necessarily associated, it is iltizām. For example, 'man' implies 'capable of writing' even though that is not part of the definition.
The connection is by mental association.
5
Apply to an Islamic example
Consider the word 'ṣalāh' (prayer). By muṭābaqa it signifies the entire act of worship. By taḍammun it signifies the part 'rukuʿ' (bowing). By iltizām it signifies 'submission' (from the root meaning).
This shows nuance in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التصورات: بيان الدلالة وتعريف أقسامها. فصل : دلالة اللفظ على تمام ما وضع له 'مطابقة'، وعلى جزئه 'تضمن'، وعلى الخارج 'التزام'. قوله : دلالة اللفظ قد علمت أن نظر المنطقي بالذات إنما هو في المعرف والحجة، وهما من قبيل المعاني لا الألفاظ، إلا أنه كما يتعارف ذكر الحد. كيف: اعلم أن الترتيب في المعرف هو أن يقدم العام على الخاص وفي الحجة أن يقدم الصغرى على الكبرى، والترتيب على الأول استحساني، وفي الثاني ضروري، وقوله: 'ينبغي' شامل لهما؛ ولذا آثره على 'يجب'. لأنها فإنك إذا قلت: العالم حادث، فمنعه الخصم، ثم إذا استدللت عليه بأن العالم متغير وكل متغير حادث، فقد غلبت عليه، فالاستدلال عليه سبب للغلبة، واسمها في اللغة 'الحجة'، فسمي باسمه، فهذه التسمية من قبيل تسمية السبب باسم المسبب. قد علمت دفع لما يقال إن المنطقي إنما يبحث عن المعرّف والحجة، وهما من أقسام المعاني دون الألفاظ، فإيراد مباحث الألفاظ في هذا الفن لا معنى له؛ لعدم كونه من وظائفه، وتقرير الدفع: إيراد مباحث الألفاظ في هذا الفن ليس باعتبار أن المنطقي يبحث عنها، بل ليعين على الإفادة والاستفادة، كما أن إيراد ذكر الأمور الثلاثة في المقدمة؛ لإفادة البصيرة في الشروع أو إزاحة لما يتوهم من أن مباحث الألفاظ مقاصد بالذات لإيرادها في المقاصد بعد المقدمة. وحاصل الإزاحة أنها مقصودة بالعرض، وإيرادها في المقاصد لشدة الاتصال بين الألفاظ والمعاني. ذكر الحد والصواب ذكر الرسم، اللهم إلا أن يراد الرسم على ما هو مذهب أهل العربية من إطلاق الحد على الأقسام الأربعة من الحد والرسم التام والناقص للمعرف فافهم (عبد) لعل قوله: 'فافهم' إيماء إلى أن الصواب ليس بصواب؛ لأن الحد أعلى وأفضل من الرسم وهو في المعاني الاصطلاحية سهل؛ لأنه ما فرض فيه ذاتي فهو جنس إن اشترك في الماهية ،وغيرها وفصل إن ميزها عن غيرها وما فرض فيه عرضي فهو خاصة إذا اختص بحقيقة واحدة وإلا فعرض عام ، ومهما أمكن ذكر الأعلى والأفضل لا ينبغي أن يذكر الأدنى. (تحفه)
Concepts: Explanation of signification and definition of its divisions. Section: The signification of a word of its whole meaning is 'congruence', of a part is 'inclusion', and of something external is 'commitment'. His statement: 'The signification of a word' has taught that the logician's direct consideration is only of the definition and the proof, and they are of the category of meanings, not words, except that it is customary to mention the definition. How: Know that the order in the definition is to present the general before the specific, and in the proof is to present the minor before the major, and the order in the first is commendable, and in the second necessary, and his statement 'ought' includes both; therefore he preferred it over 'must'. Because if you say: 'The world is originated', and the opponent denies it, then if you adduce evidence by saying 'The world is changing and everything changing is originated', you have overcome him; so the inference is a cause for overcoming, and its name in language is 'al-ḥujja' (proof), so it is named after it, and this naming is of the type of naming a cause after its effect. It has been taught: a repudiation of what is said that the logician only investigates the definition and the proof, and they are among the divisions of meanings, not words, so bringing discussions of words in this art has no meaning, because it is not among its functions. The explanation of the repudiation: The introduction of discussions of words in this art is not because the logician investigates them, but rather to aid communication and understanding, just as mentioning the three matters in the introduction is to give insight in the beginning, or to remove the misconception that discussions of words are direct objectives because they are introduced in the aims after the introduction. The gist of the removal is that they are intended secondarily, and their introduction in the aims is due to the intense connection between words and meanings. He mentioned the definition (ḥadd) whereas the correct thing is to mention the description (rasm), unless the description is intended according to the doctrine of the Arabic grammarians who apply the term 'definition' to the four divisions: the essential definition, the complete description, and the incomplete description of the definition, so understand. (ʿAbd) Perhaps his statement 'so understand' is a hint that the correct is not correct, because the definition is higher and better than the description, and it is easy in conventional meanings; because what is posited as essential is genus if it participates in the essence, and differentia if it distinguishes it from others, and what is posited as accidental is a property if it is specific to one reality, otherwise it is a common accident. And whenever it is possible to mention the higher and better, it is not appropriate to mention the lower. (Tuḥfa)
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage explains the three types of verbal signification (dalāla) and defends the inclusion of linguistic discussions in logic. It begins by defining the three divisions: muṭābaqa (congruence) when a word signifies its entire meaning, taḍammun (inclusion) when it signifies a part, and iltizām (commitment) when it signifies something external. The author then addresses a potential objection: since logic primarily deals with meanings (definitions and proofs), why discuss words? The response is that linguistic discussions aid communication (ifāda wa istifāda) and are introduced not as direct objectives but as secondary, due to the strong connection between words and meanings. The passage also includes a note on the preference of ḥadd (essential definition) over rasm (descriptive definition), advising that when possible, the higher form should be used. The marginalia from ʿAbd and Tuḥfa further elaborate this point, noting that the conventional practice is to use ḥadd, which includes genus and differentia, while rasm is less precise.

Key Takeaway
Verbal signification is divided into congruence (whole), inclusion (part), and commitment (external).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Find an example of taḍammun in the definition of 'iman' (faith) as 'belief in the heart, speech on the tongue, and action of the limbs' - for instance, 'belief in the heart' is a part signified by taḍammun.

Why Logic Discusses Words: Secondary Aims and Hadd vs Rasm
Author defends inclusion of word-discussions and prefers ḥadd over rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why logicians discuss words despite logic being about meanings, and distinguish between ḥadd (essential definition) and rasm (description).

Core Idea
Logic discusses words not directly, but to aid communication, and prefers ḥadd over rasm.

If logic is about meanings and arguments, why do logic books start with words? The author answers this objection and also clarifies the preferred form of definition: ḥadd is superior to rasm. In this lesson, we unpack these important meta-logical points.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection states: logic's subject is definitions and proofs, which are meanings, not words. So why discuss words?
This is a common initial confusion.
2
Understand the response
The author replies that linguistic discussions are introduced secondarily to aid communication (ifāda wa istifāda), not as primary objectives. They are necessary because words carry meanings.
Like the introduction of preliminary topics in any science.
3
Recognize the preference for ḥadd
The author notes that when defining, one should use ḥadd (essential definition: genus + differentia) over rasm (description using accidents), because ḥadd is higher and more precise.
This reflects a value judgment in the tradition.
4
Examine the exception for grammarians
The marginalia (ʿAbd and Tuḥfa) mention that grammarians sometimes call rasm by the term 'ḥadd', but the logician should stick to the stricter sense.
This shows variation between disciplines.
5
Apply to an Islamic science example
In fiqh, defining 'ṣalāh' as 'ritual prayers with specific actions' (rasm) is lower than defining it as 'an act of worship consisting of standing, bowing, prostrating, etc.' (ḥadd). The latter includes essential constituents.
The preferred definition in logic is the essential one.

The gist of the removal is that they are intended secondarily, and their introduction in the aims is due to the intense connection between words and meanings. He mentioned the definition (ḥadd) whereas the correct thing is to mention the description (rasm), unless the description is intended according to the doctrine of the Arabic grammarians who apply the term 'definition' to the four divisions: the essential definition, the complete description, and the incomplete description of the definition, so understand. (ʿAbd) Perhaps his statement 'so understand' is a hint that the correct is not correct, because the definition is higher and better than the description, and it is easy in conventional meanings; because what is posited as essential is genus if it participates in the essence, and differentia if it distinguishes it from others, and what is posited as accidental is a property if it is specific to one reality, otherwise it is a common accident. And whenever it is possible to mention the higher and better, it is not appropriate to mention the lower. (Tuḥfa)
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage explains the three types of verbal signification (dalāla) and defends the inclusion of linguistic discussions in logic. It begins by defining the three divisions: muṭābaqa (congruence) when a word signifies its entire meaning, taḍammun (inclusion) when it signifies a part, and iltizām (commitment) when it signifies something external. The author then addresses a potential objection: since logic primarily deals with meanings (definitions and proofs), why discuss words? The response is that linguistic discussions aid communication (ifāda wa istifāda) and are introduced not as direct objectives but as secondary, due to the strong connection between words and meanings. The passage also includes a note on the preference of ḥadd (essential definition) over rasm (descriptive definition), advising that when possible, the higher form should be used. The marginalia from ʿAbd and Tuḥfa further elaborate this point, noting that the conventional practice is to use ḥadd, which includes genus and differentia, while rasm is less precise.

Key Terms

الحجة
الحد
الرسم

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because words are the primary subject of logic.
